Proof that Allah Does Not Need a Substratum
Proof that Allah does not need a substratum and is not an attribute.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the logical proof that Allah is a self-subsistent essence and does not require a substratum, and why He cannot be an attribute.

Core Idea
Allah is not an attribute because attributes cannot accept other attributes.

This passage presents a rigorous proof from Imam Dardir that Allah is not an attribute needing a substratum. The argument is built on the impossibility of an attribute being characterized by another attribute, which would lead to contradictions and infinite regress. Since Allah possesses positive attributes, He cannot be an attribute of another; thus, He must be a self-subsistent essence.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once to appreciate its structure. Then read the literal translation to understand the flow of the argument.
Notice the conditional 'if...then' structure at the beginning.
2
Identify the main conditional claim
Locate the statement: if Allah needed a substratum, He would be an attribute. Understand why this is the starting point of the proof.
This is the hypothesis to be refuted.
3
Follow the reductio argument
Trace the reasoning that shows why being an attribute is impossible: because an attribute cannot accept another attribute, leading to infinite regress and contradictions.
Focus on the examples of knowledge and power.
4
Connect to positive attributes
Notice that the proof uses the fact that Allah has positive attributes (knowledge, power, will). Since these subsist in Him, He cannot be an attribute of another.
This is the crucial link to the conclusion.
5
Reach the conclusion
Understand that therefore, Allah is a self-subsistent essence and does not need a substratum. This is the sought result.
The proof is complete.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أما أنه تعالى لا يفتقر إلى محل يقوم به قيامَ الصَّفةِ بموصوفها، فلأنه لو افتقر إلى ذلك لكان صفة لا ذاتا، إذ الذاتُ لا تقوم بالذاتِ، لكن كَونه تعالى صِفَةً مُحالٌ، إذ لو كان صفةً لاستحال قيام الصفات الثبوتية - كالعِلْمِ والقدرة والإرادة- به تعالى، إذ الصفة لا تقبل صفةٌ أخرى تقوم بها، وإلا لَزِمَ أنْ لا تخلو عنها، أو عن مِثلِها، أو عن ضدها، ويلزم مثل ذلك في الأخرى التي قامت بها، وهكذا، إذ القَبولُ أَمْرٌ نَفْسِي لا بُدَّ أَنْ يَتَّحِدَ بَينَ المُتَمائِلِينِ أو المتماثلات، وهو مُحالٌ لِما يلزَمُ عليهِ مِنَ اتِّصافِ الصفة يمثلها أو بضدّها أو بخلافها، فيكونُ العِلْمُ عالما وجاهِلا وقادِرًا، وكذا العكْسُ، باطل، ومِنْ دخولِ ما لا نهاية له مِنَ الصَّفاتِ الوُجوديّة. على أنَّ الصِّفةَ لو اتَّصَفتْ بأُخرى للزِمَ الترجيحُ بلا مُرَجّح، إذ جعلُ إحداهما موصوفة والأُخْرى صفةً لها دون أن تكونَ صفةً للذات التي قامت بها الموصوفة، ودون أن تكون الموصوفة الصِّفةُ للأخرى تحكُمْ، فَليُتَأَمَّلْ. وهو تعالى قد ثبت أنه قامت به الصفاتُ الثَّبوتيّةُ، فلا يكونُ صِفةٌ لغَيره، فوجَبَ أن يكونَ ذاتا فلا يفْتَقِرُ إلى محلّه، وهو المطلوب.
As for His being exalted not needing a substratum in which He subsists as the subsistence of an attribute in its possessor, then because if He needed that, He would be an attribute, not a self-subsistent essence, for the self-subsistent essence does not subsist in a self-subsistent essence. But His being exalted an attribute is impossible, because if He were an attribute, the subsistence of the positive attributes—such as knowledge, power, and will—in Him exalted would be impossible, for the attribute does not accept another attribute subsisting in it. Otherwise, it would necessitate that it would not be devoid of it, or of its like, or of its opposite, and similar would be necessitated in the other attribute that subsisted in it, and so on. For acceptance is a self-subsistent matter that must unite between similar things, and that is impossible because of what would follow from it of the characterization of the attribute by its like, its opposite, or its contrary, so knowledge would be knowing, ignorant, and powerful, and likewise the reverse—false. And from the entering of infinite existential attributes. Moreover, if an attribute were characterized by another, it would necessitate preponderance without a preponderator, since making one of them described and the other an attribute for it without it being an attribute of the essence in which the described one subsisted, and without the described attribute having governance over the other, so let it be contemplated. And He exalted has been established that the positive attributes subsist in Him, so He is not an attribute for another. Therefore, it is necessary that He be a self-subsistent essence, and so He does not need a substratum—that is what is sought.
Source pages p. 74

Commentary
This passage is a proof by the author that Allah does not need a substratum (mahall) in which He subsists like an attribute subsists in its possessor. The argument proceeds as follows: If Allah needed a substratum, He would be an attribute (sifah) and not a self-subsistent essence (dhat). However, it is impossible for Allah to be an attribute because if He were an attribute, the positive attributes like knowledge, power, and will could not subsist in Him. This is because an attribute cannot accept another attribute subsisting in it; if it did, it would be subject to an infinite regress and would necessitate that an attribute be characterized by its like or opposite, leading to contradictions such as knowledge being both knowing and ignorant. Moreover, the attribute would need a preponderator to determine which attribute is the subject and which is the predicate, which would require a preponderator without a preponderant. Since it is established that the positive attributes do subsist in Allah, He cannot be an attribute of another. Therefore, He must be a self-subsistent essence and thus does not need a substratum. This is the conclusion.

Key Terms
ذات
صفة
محل
قيام
اتصاف
ترجيح بلا مرجح
صفات ثبوتية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: If Allah has attributes, He must be like other beings that have attributes and require a substratum.
Correction: Allah is not an accident subsisting in a substratum; He is a self-subsistent essence. The fact that He has attributes proves He is not an attribute of another.

Checkpoint
According to the author, why is it impossible for Allah to be an attribute?
A) Because an attribute cannot exist without a substratum
B) Because an attribute cannot accept another attribute subsisting in it
C) Because attributes are eternal
D) Because Allah is simple

Key Takeaway
Allah is a self-subsistent essence who does not need a substratum; the fact that He has attributes proves He cannot be an attribute of another.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If Allah were an attribute of something else, how would that affect your reliance on Him as the ultimate reality? Can you identify any area in your life where you are effectively treating something other than Allah as the substratum of your trust?
?
The proof shows that attributes cannot accept other attributes. Are there any 'attributes' of your own character—like knowledge or power—that you have allowed to become ends in themselves, rather than being anchored in your dependence on Allah?
?
If Allah does not need a substratum, He is entirely self-sufficient. How does this truth confront your own tendencies toward self-sufficiency? In what concrete way will you acknowledge your dependence on Him today?

The Impossibility of Union (Ittihad) with God
Proof that union with God is impossible.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the logical proof that God cannot unite with any other being, based on the three scenarios of attempted union.

Core Idea
Two cannot become one without ceasing to be two.

Imam Dardir now applies the doctrine of God's self-subsistence to refute the idea that God can unite with creation. He presents a concise logical argument that union is impossible by examining what would happen if two things attempted to become one. This argument is foundational for understanding God's absolute uniqueness.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the source passage on union carefully. Notice how it begins by linking to the previous conclusion that God is self-subsistent.
Pay attention to the three scenarios in the proof.
2
Identify the three scenarios
The author lists three possibilities when two things attempt to unite. List them in your mind: both remain, both cease, or one ceases.
3
Understand why each fails
For each scenario, see why it cannot result in a true union. The third scenario leads to a contradiction involving the necessary and possible.
Focus on the logical necessity of the conclusion.
4
Connect to self-subsistence
Reflect on how God's self-subsistence (qiyam bi-nafs) makes union impossible. Union would imply dependence or change.
This reinforces God's independence.
5
Check your understanding
Answer the checkpoint question to test your grasp of the argument.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
إذا علمت أنه يجب له تعالى قيامه بنفسه تعلم أنه تعالى يستحيل في حقه أن يتحد بغيره، أو يحل فيه. أما الأول فلما تقرر من امتناع اتحاد الاثنين ما داما اثنين، لأن أحدهما إذا اتحد بالآخر فإن بقي على حالهما فهما اثنان لا واحد فلا اتحاد ، وإن عدما كان الموجود غيرهما، وإن عدم أحدهما دون الآخر امتنع الاتحاد لأن المعدوم لا يكون عين الموجود، ولأنه يلزم أن يكون الواجب هو الممكن. والممكن هو الواجب، وذلك محال بالضرورة. وأما الثاني فلأوجه: أحدها: أن الحال في الشيء يفتقر إليه في الجملة سواء كان حلول جسم في مكان، أو عرض في جوهر أو صورة في مادة كما هو رأي الحكماء، أو صفة في موصوف كصفان المجردات، والافتقار إلى الغير ينافي الوجود الذاتي. ثانيها : أن الحلول في الغير إن لم يكن صفة كمال وجب نفيه عن الواجب، وإن كان صفة كمال لزم كون الواجب مستكملا بالغير وهو باطل باتفاق ثالثها: أنه تعالى لو حل في شيء لزم تحيزه ، وكما امتنع الحلول والاتحاد على ذاته تعالى امتنع على صفاته أيضا، بل هي أولى بالامتناع لاستحالة انتقال الصفة عن الذات.
When you know that self-subsistence is necessary for Him, may He be exalted, you know that it is impossible for Him, may He be exalted, to unite with another, or to indwell it. As for the first [impossibility of union], it is because it is established that union of two things is impossible as long as they are two; for if one of them unites with the other, then if they remain as they were, they are two, not one, so no union. If they both cease to exist, what exists is other than them. If one of them ceases to exist without the other, union is impossible because what is non-existent cannot be identical with what exists, and because it would necessitate that the necessary [being] is the possible, and the possible is the necessary—and that is impossible of necessity. As for the second [indwelling], it has several aspects: one of them: that the one indwelling in a thing depends upon it in some way, whether it is the indwelling of a body in a place, or an accident in a substance, or a form in matter as is the view of the philosophers, or an attribute in a described thing like attributes of incorporeal beings; and dependency upon another contradicts self-existent being. Second: if indwelling in another is not a perfection, it must be negated of the Necessary [Being]; and if it were a perfection, it would necessitate that the Necessary [Being] is perfected by another—which is false by consensus. Third: that if He, exalted, were to indwell in something, it would necessitate that He be located in space. And just as indwelling and union are impossible for His essence, exalted, so too they are impossible for His attributes; rather, they are more deserving of impossibility due to the impossibility of an attribute transferring from the essence.
Source pages p. 75

Commentary
This passage provides proofs for the impossibility of God uniting with or indwelling any created thing. It is structured as a conditional statement: once you know that God is self-subsistent (qā'im bi-nafsihi), you understand that union (ittihad) and indwelling (hulul) are impossible for Him. The author then gives arguments for each. For the impossibility of union: (1) If two things remain as they are after union, they are still two, not one, so no union occurred. (2) If both cease to exist, something else exists. (3) If only one ceases, the non-existent cannot be identical with the existent, and it would entail that the Necessary (wājib) is the possible (mumkin), which is absurd. For the impossibility of indwelling, three reasons are given: (a) The indwelling entity depends on the indwelt thing, contradicting God's self-existence. (b) Indwelling is either not a perfection (so must be negated) or is a perfection (then God would be perfected by another, impossible by consensus). (c) Indwelling would necessitate corporeality (tahayyuz). The author concludes that just as union and indwelling are impossible for God's essence, they are even more impossible for His attributes, because attributes cannot transfer to another subject.

Key Terms
الاتحاد
القيام بالنفس
الواجب
الممكن

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That God can unite with a holy person or a place, as in the concept of incarnation.
Correction: The argument shows that union is impossible because it always leads to contradiction. God's self-subsistence prevents any dependency on another.

Checkpoint
Why does the author argue that union (ittihad) is impossible between two things?
A) Because one must annihilate the other
B) Because if both remain, they are still two
C) Because union requires a common substratum
D) Because union is a created attribute

Key Takeaway
Union with God is logically impossible because it leads to contradictions in all possible scenarios.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You have learned that union with God is logically impossible. Do you still seek to 'feel' one with God through spiritual experiences? How does this truth reshape your pursuit of closeness to Him? Will you now focus on submission and obedience rather than mystical merging?
?
This passage shows that you cannot become God or merge with Him. Are you truly content being a servant, or do you secretly desire a higher status? Commit today to embracing your role as a created being and worshipping Him as your Lord.
?
If union is impossible, then what does it mean for God to be 'close' to you as mentioned in the Qur'an (e.g., 'And We are closer to him than his jugular vein')? Does this argument challenge your previous understanding? Will you seek the correct Islamic interpretation of divine nearness?

The Impossibility of Indwelling (Hulul) in God
Proof that indwelling (hulul) with God is impossible.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the three reasons why indwelling (hulul) is impossible for God, based on His self-subsistence and perfection.

Core Idea
Indwelling implies dependence, which contradicts God's self-sufficiency.

Having established that union is impossible, Imam Dardir now turns to indwelling (hulul). He provides three distinct arguments: indwelling implies dependence on the host; if it is not a perfection, it must be denied; if it is a perfection, it would mean God is perfected by another; and indwelling requires spatial location. These arguments reinforce God's absolute transcendence.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the indwelling passage, noting the three reasons given. The opening reminds us of the link to self-subsistence.
2
Understand the first reason
The first reason: indwelling implies dependency. Any being that indwells another depends on it in some way, which contradicts God's self-subsistence.
Examples include a body in a place or an accident in a substance.
3
Understand the second reason
The second reason uses a dichotomy: if indwelling is not a perfection, it must be negated of God; if it is a perfection, God would be perfected by another, which is false by consensus.
This shows God's perfection cannot derive from another.
4
Understand the third reason
The third reason: indwelling would necessitate spatial location (tahayyuz), which is impossible for a non-corporeal being.
This ties to God's transcendence above physical attributes.
5
Apply to God's attributes
Note the author's conclusion: just as indwelling and union are impossible for God's essence, they are even more impossible for His attributes, which cannot transfer.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

When you know that self-subsistence is necessary for Him, may He be exalted, you know that it is impossible for Him, may He be exalted, to unite with another, or to indwell it. As for the first [impossibility of union], it is because it is established that union of two things is impossible as long as they are two; for if one of them unites with the other, then if they remain as they were, they are two, not one, so no union. If they both cease to exist, what exists is other than them. If one of them ceases to exist without the other, union is impossible because what is non-existent cannot be identical with what exists, and because it would necessitate that the necessary [being] is the possible, and the possible is the necessary—and that is impossible of necessity. As for the second [indwelling], it has several aspects: one of them: that the one indwelling in a thing depends upon it in some way, whether it is the indwelling of a body in a place, or an accident in a substance, or a form in matter as is the view of the philosophers, or an attribute in a described thing like attributes of incorporeal beings; and dependency upon another contradicts self-existent being. Second: if indwelling in another is not a perfection, it must be negated of the Necessary [Being]; and if it were a perfection, it would necessitate that the Necessary [Being] is perfected by another—which is false by consensus. Third: that if He, exalted, were to indwell in something, it would necessitate that He be located in space. And just as indwelling and union are impossible for His essence, exalted, so too they are impossible for His attributes; rather, they are more deserving of impossibility due to the impossibility of an attribute transferring from the essence.

Commentary
This passage provides proofs for the impossibility of God uniting with or indwelling any created thing. The Attribute of Mukhalafa: God's Complete Difference from Creation
Definition of the fourth negative attribute with an enumerated list of specific negations.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that the attribute of mukhalafa means God is absolutely unlike any created thing in every respect, and that this is expressed through a series of specific negations.

Core Idea
God is not like anything, and nothing is like Him.

We now turn to the fourth negative attribute: 'mukhalafa' or 'being different from creation.' This is a central tenet of Islamic theology—God's absolute transcendence. The author defines it as non-conformity to any created thing, and then lists many specific qualities that are denied of God. Each negation reinforces the core idea that God is beyond all categories of His creation.

Guided Path
1
Read the definition of mukhalafa.
Open with the Arabic: 'ورابع الصفات السلبية تخالف للغير...' and its translation. Notice that the author first gives a general meaning: 'non-conformity to any of created things.'
This is the conceptual foundation.
2
Examine the list of negations.
Go through each item in the list: not a substance, not a body, not an accident, not moving or still, etc. Each one reinforces that God cannot be described by categories that apply to creation.
Pay attention to both positive-like attributes (e.g., substance) and relational attributes (e.g., above/below).
3
Reflect on the purpose of negation.
Ask yourself: why is it necessary to deny so many things? The answer is that affirming any of them would imply similarity between God and creation. Negation protects God's absolute uniqueness.
This is a key principle in negative theology (sifāt salbiyya).
4
Connect to the common misunderstanding.
Some might think that denying these attributes means God has their opposites (e.g., not big means He must be small). But Islamic theology teaches that God is free from all limitations—He is neither big nor small in the created sense.
The passage's silence on opposites is intentional.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ورابعُ الصِّفاتِ السلبية (تَخَالُفٌ للغَيرِ) أَيْ: مخالفتُه تعالى لغَيرِه مِنَ الحوادث. المخالفة (٢) ومعناها: عدم الموافقة لشَيْءٍ مِنَ الحوادثِ، فَلَيسَ تعالى بجوهر ("") ولا جسم (۳) اللحوادث ولا عرَض (٤) ولا مُتَحَرِّك ولا ساكن، ولا يوصف تعالى بالكِبَرِ ولا بالصَّغَرِ، ولا بالفوقية ولا بالتحتيّة، ولا بالحلول (0) في الأمكنة)، ولا بالاتحاد، ولا بالاتصال ولا بالانفصال ()، ولا باليمين ولا بالشمال، ولا بالخلف ولا بالأمام، =
And the fourth of the negative attributes is 'oppositeness to the other' (takhāluf lil-ghayr), i.e., His, exalted, being different from what is other than Him of created things. Al-mukhālafa (oppositeness) and its meaning is: non-conformity to any of created things. So He, exalted, is not a substance, nor a body, nor an accident, nor moving nor still, nor is He described with bigness nor smallness, nor with being above nor below, nor with indwelling in places, nor with union, nor with connection nor disconnection, nor with right nor left, nor with front nor back, =
Source pages p. 76

Commentary
This passage defines the fourth of the negative attributes (al-ṣifāt al-salbiyya): 'takhāluf lil-ghayr', meaning God's being different from all created things. The author explains that 'mukhālafa' means non-conformity to any created thing. He then provides a list of specific negations that illustrate this attribute: God is not a substance (jawhar), not a body (jism), not an accident (ʿaraḍ), not moving or still, not described with size (big or small), not with spatial location (above/below), not with indwelling (ḥulūl) in places, not with union (ittiḥād), not with connection or disconnection, not with directions (right, left, front, back). The list continues on the next page (indicated by the '=' sign). This enumeration shows that God transcends all categories applicable to created, contingent beings.

Key Terms
المخالفة
الذات
صفة سلبية
جوهر
جسم
عرض
حلول
اتحاد

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Negating these attributes means God has their opposites (e.g., not big means He is small).
Correction: Islamic theology teaches that God is free from all limitations—He is neither big nor small in the created sense. Negation affirms His absolute transcendence beyond all human categories.

Checkpoint
What does the attribute 'mukhālafa lil-ḥawādith' mean according to the passage?
A) God is different only in some ways from creation
B) God is not similar to any created thing in any way
C) God is unlike creation in essence but like it in attributes
D) God is completely unknown

Key Takeaway
The attribute of mukhalafa establishes that God is absolutely unlike any created thing, as shown by the negation of all categories that apply to contingent beings.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You have just read that God does not dwell in any place, nor is He connected or disconnected. When you pray, where do you imagine God to be? How does your mental image of God need to change so that you worship Him as He truly is—beyond all space and direction?
?
If God is not like anything you have ever seen, heard, or imagined, how can you sincerely worship Him without reducing Him to a mental picture? What specific step will you take today to purify your conception of God?
?
The list of negations includes 'not moving nor still'. Yet you often speak of God's 'actions' in creation. How can you reconcile your belief that God acts without attributing movement to Him? Will you commit to studying the divine attributes more deeply so that your speech about God remains free of creaturely likeness?

Divine Oneness: Negating Multiplicity in Essence, Attributes, and Actions
Dardeer defines oneness and explains its three aspects: essence, attributes, actions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the meaning of divine oneness (wahdāniyya) as the negation of multiplicity in Allah's essence, attributes, and actions.

Core Idea
Wahdāniyya is not just saying 'One' but negating all multiplicity in God.

Dardeer now introduces the fifth negative attribute: oneness. He explains that this attribute goes beyond simply affirming that God is one; it negates any form of multiplicity in His essence, attributes, and actions. This passage breaks down each domain to show how God's uniqueness is absolute.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice that Dardeer uses a very systematic, enumerative style.
2
Identify the three aspects of oneness
The passage presents three domains where multiplicity is negated: essence, attributes, and actions. Find where each is discussed and note what is being negated in each case.
These three aspects are explicit in the text.
3
Understand negation in essence
Focus on the first part: oneness of essence negates composition (continuous quantity) and the existence of a similar essence (discrete quantity). This means God is not made of parts and there is no other being like Him in essence.
The terms 'continuous' and 'discrete' quantity are key.
4
Grasp oneness in attributes
The second aspect: oneness of attributes negates multiplicity within each attribute (e.g., only one life, one knowledge) and also negates that any other being could possess divine attributes.
This means God's attributes are singular in their kind and exclusive to Him.
5
Reflect on oneness in actions
The third aspect: oneness of actions affirms that only God truly acts and has real effect; all creatures are incapable and have no independent causal power.
This is a strong denial of secondary causality in the absolute sense.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وخامسُ الصَّفاتِ السلبية (وحدانية) وهي: عبارةٌ عَنْ سَلْبِ الكثرة في الذات والصفات والأفعال، أي: عدَمُ الاثنينيّةِ في الذاتِ أي: في ذاته تعالى اتصالاً وانفصالًا. فوحدانيّةُ الذاتِ تنفي عنه تعالى الكمَّ المتَّصِلَ والمنفَصِلَ، أَيْ: تنفي العدَدَ في الذاتِ، متّصِلا كان أو منفصلا، فتنفي التركيب في ذاته تعالى، ووُجودَ ذات أخرى تُماثِلُ الذات العليّة. و الصفات تنفي - القسم الأول: الإلهيات ذاته (أو) أي: وعدَمُ الاثنينيّة فى صفاته العَليّة اتصالا أو انفصالًا أيضًا، فوحدانية تعالى الكَمَّ فيها، أي تنفي العدَدَ في حقيقة كُلِّ واحدة منها، مُتصلا كان أو مُنْفَصلًا، أى أنه تعالى له حياة واحدة، وعلم واحد وهكذا لا أكثرَ . وَلَيسَ ثَمَّ مَنْ يَتَّصِفُ بِصِفاتِ الألوهيّةِ سِواه تعالى. ٢٥ - والفعل، فالتأثير ليس إلا * للواحد القهار جَلَّ وعلا (و) وحدانيّةٌ، أي: عدَمُ الاثنينية في الفِعْلِ يعني: أنه تعالى مُتَّصِفٌ بِوَحْدانيّةِ الأفعال) ، فَلَيسَ ثَمَّ مَنْ له فِعلٌ مِنَ الأفعالِ سِواه تعالى، إِذْ كلُّ ما سواه عاجز، لا تأثير له في شَيءٍ مِنَ الأشياء.
And the fifth of the negative attributes is oneness (wahdāniyya). It is an expression for the negation of multiplicity in essence, attributes, and actions. That is, the absence of duality in the essence: in His essence, the Exalted, whether by connection or separation. So the oneness of essence negates from Him, the Exalted, continuous and discrete quantity, i.e., it negates number in the essence, whether it be connected or separate. So it negates composition in His essence, the Exalted, and the existence of another essence similar to the supreme essence. And the part on attributes: the first section: divine matters. His essence (or): i.e., the absence of duality in His supreme attributes, whether by connection or separation. So the oneness of the Exalted [negates] the quantity in them, i.e., it negates number in the reality of each one of them, whether it be connected or separate. That is, He, the Exalted, has one life, one knowledge, and so on, no more. And there is no one who is described with the attributes of divinity besides Him, the Exalted. 25 – And the action: effect is only for the One, the All-Subduer, glorified and exalted. (And) oneness, i.e., the absence of duality in action. That is, He, the Exalted, is described with oneness of actions. So there is no one who has any action among actions besides Him, the Exalted, for everything other than Him is incapable, having no effect in anything among things.
Source pages p. 77

Commentary
This passage defines the fifth negative attribute, oneness (wahdāniyya). Dardeer explains that wahdāniyya negates multiplicity in three domains: essence, attributes, and actions. For the essence, it negates both continuous multiplicity (composition from parts) and discrete multiplicity (another similar essence). For the attributes, it negates multiplicity within each attribute (e.g., multiple lives) and also negates that anyone else could share God's attributes. For the actions, it affirms that only God creates and has real effect; all others are incapable. The passage includes a poetic line emphasizing that effect belongs only to the One, the All-Subduer.

Correction: The passage explicitly states that no one other than God has any effect (lā ta'thīr lahu fī shay'in min al-ashyā'). This denies any true causal power in creatures.

The passage says oneness of actions means nothing besides Allah has any effect. In your daily life, where do you functionally deny this—by worrying about outcomes, trusting your own plans, or resenting someone's influence? Will you commit to repeating 'there is no effect except from Allah' before your next anxious thought?
?
You affirm that Allah's essence has no composition and no equal. But do you ever treat your own ego, status, or possessions as independent sources of worth? If Allah alone is one in essence, what must you strip away from your sense of self to align with that truth?

Definition of Unity in Acts (Wahdaniyya al-Fi'l)
Dardeer defines divine unity in acts and denies effective power to others.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand what unity in acts (waḥdāniyya al-fiʿl) means and why it entails that only Allah has effective power.

Core Idea
Only Allah truly acts; all others are incapable.

Dardeer now turns to the third dimension of divine unity: unity in acts. This principle clarifies that all effective power belongs solely to Allah, and every creature is inherently powerless. The passage dismantles any notion of independent secondary causality.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation carefully.
Read the Arabic passage once through, then its translation. Notice how the couplet and commentary flow together.
The passage begins with a couplet line, then the commentator unpacks it.
2
Identify the key claim about effectiveness.
Find the statement that effective power (al-tathīr) is only for Allah. Understand that this negates any real effect by creatures.
The word 'tathīr' is central.
3
Reflect on the implication for all creatures.
The passage explicitly says all other than Allah are 'incapable' (ʿājiz) and have no effect. Consider what this means for everyday causality.
This does not deny secondary causes as means, but denies independent power.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والفعل، فالتأثير ليس إلا * للواحد القهار جَلَّ وعلا (و) وحدانيّة، أي: عدَمُ الاثنينية في (الفِعْلِ) يعني: أنه تعالى مُتَّصِفٌ بِوَحْدانيّةِ الأفعال) ، فلَيسَ ثَمَّ مَنْ له فِعلٌ مِنَ الأفعالِ سِواه تعالى، إِذْ كلُّ ما سواه عاجز، لا تأثير له في شَيءٍ ) مِنَ الأشياء.
And the act: so effective power (al-tathīr) is not except for the One, the Subduer (al-wāḥid al-qahhār), may He be glorified and exalted. And unity (waḥdāniyya), i.e., absence of duality in the act, meaning that He, exalted, is described with unity of acts. So there is no one who has any act from the acts besides Him, exalted, for everything other than Him is incapable, having no effect in anything from the things.
Source pages p. 78

Commentary
This passage defines the third type of divine unity, namely unity in acts (waḥdāniyya al-fiʿl). It begins by quoting the couplet: 'And the act: so effective power is not except for the One, the Subduer.' The commentator explains that unity here means denial of duality in action: that Allah alone is truly described as having effective acts. No other being has any real effect; all others are inherently incapable and have no influence over anything. This establishes that all causality is from Allah alone.

Key Terms

Misconception: Some think unity in acts denies secondary causality entirely, meaning that created things have no role at all.
Correction: Unity in acts denies independent creation and effect, but it does not deny that Allah uses secondary causes as means. Creatures are instruments, not independent agents.

Key Takeaway
Unity in acts means that no being other than Allah has any true effect; all causality is from Allah alone.

The passage says 'كل ما سواه عاجز' (everything other than Him is incapable). Think of a moment you felt pride in an achievement. Does your heart truly accept that your success was only through Allah's effect, or do you secretly credit yourself? What step will you take tomorrow to affirm Allah's sole effective power in a specific action?
?

Human Acts Are Created by Allah Alone
Dardeer states that all human actions are created by Allah, not by human power.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why all human voluntary actions are directly created by Allah and how this aligns with the Ash'ari concept of acquisition (kasb).

Core Idea
True creative power belongs only to Allah; human acts are His creation.

In this passage, Imam Dardeer applies the doctrine of divine unity to the question of human actions. He argues that since Allah alone possesses the power to bring things from non-existence into existence, no human power can have any real effect. This establishes the Ash'ari position that all human actions are created by Allah, while still affirming human accountability through the concept of acquisition (kasb). Let's examine his reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice how Dardeer uses the Quranic verse to seal his argument.
2
Identify the two main parts
The passage has two clear sections: first, the general principle that tathīr (effective power) is only for Allah; second, the application to human actions, concluding with a Quranic proof.
These two parts are connected by the logic of divine unity.
3
Understand the implication for human responsibility
If our power has no effect, how are we accountable? Ash'aris answer with kasb (acquisition). The passage does not elaborate on kasb, but it sets the foundation: the act is Allah's creation, the human acquires it.
This prevents misunderstanding that humans are mere puppets.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإذا علمت أنه تعالى يجب له الوَحْدانيّةُ (فالتأثير) الاختراعُ والإيجاد للأشياء مِنَ العدَمِ (لَيسَ) أي: لا يصِحُ لأحَدٍ (إلا للواحِدِ القَهَّارِ) وحدَه (جل وعلا). فلا تأثيرَ لقُدرتِنا في شَيْءٍ مِنْ أفعالنا الاختيارية، كالحركات والسكنات والقيام والقعود ونحو ذلك، بل جميع ذلك مخلوق له سبحانه وتعالى بلا واسطة، كما أن قدرتنا مخلوقةٌ لَه تعالى، ﴿ وَاللَّهُ خَلَقَكُمْ وَمَا تَعْمَلُونَ ﴾ أَيْ : وخَلَقَ عَمَلَكم .
And when you know that He, exalted, must have unity, then the effective power (al-tathīr) — i.e., invention and bringing-into-existence of things from nothing — is not correct for anyone except the One, the Subduer (al-wāḥid al-qahhār) alone, may He be glorified and exalted. So there is no effect for our power in any of our voluntary actions, like movements and rests, standing and sitting, and the like. Rather, all of that is created by Him, glorified and exalted, without any intermediary, just as our power is created by Him, exalted. [And He said] 'And Allah created you and what you do' (Quran 37:96), i.e., He created your action.
Source pages p. 79

Commentary
This passage applies the principle of unity in acts to human actions. The author states that since Allah alone has true effective power (tathīr) — meaning invention and creation from nothing — no one else can have any real effect. Human power has no influence whatsoever on our voluntary actions such as movements, rest, sitting, standing. All such actions are directly created by Allah without mediation, just as our power itself is created. He cites the verse 'And Allah created you and what you do' to support this, interpreting 'what you do' as 'your action' (i.e., the act itself is created). This is the Ash'ari position on kasb (acquisition): the act is created by Allah, and the human acquires it.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that if Allah creates our actions, then humans have no free will and are not responsible.
Correction: Ash'aris affirm that although Allah creates the act, humans acquire it through intention (kasb), which is the basis of moral responsibility. The passage does not discuss kasb but lays the foundation that the act is created, not that humans are coerced.

Key Takeaway
All human voluntary actions are directly created by Allah, and human power has no creative effect, but humans acquire these actions and are accountable.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If you truly believed that every movement you make, even the decision to stand or sit, is created directly by Allah without any effective power from you, how would your sense of reliance on Him change today? Would you still worry about your own planning and effort as if they were independent?
?
Do you actually live as if your actions are created by you, not by Allah? When you succeed, do you credit your own ability? When you fail, do you blame yourself? How does this verse (Quran 37:96) force you to reconsider where you place your trust?
?
If your power itself is a creature of Allah, then what right do you have to be arrogant about any accomplishment? Will you today, before sleeping, ask Allah to forgive the moments you acted as though you were the creator of your own deeds?

Ruling on Jabriyya and Qadariyya
Author rules on Jabriyya and Qadariyya sects.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the Jabriyya are considered disbelievers and why the Qadariyya are not, according to the Ash'ari perspective.

Core Idea
Extreme compulsion nullifies religious obligation; Qadariyya's error is less severe.

This lesson examines the theological rulings on two extreme sects: the Jabriyya, who deny human agency entirely, and the Qadariyya, who overemphasize it. The author clarifies why the former are outright disbelievers while the latter, despite their error, are not.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Note the analogy of the thread and the mention of the two sects.
Pay attention to the phrase 'باللأم' which may need verification.
2
Identify the two sects and their positions
Locate where the author describes the Qadariyya belief (effect of originated power) and the Jabriyya belief (negation of choice).
3
Understand the reasoning for each ruling
The author gives a reason for the Jabriyya being kuffar (negation of taklif) and for the Qadariyya not being kuffar (they still affirm Allah's creation of power and will).
Consider why the author says 'the correct view is their non-disbelief'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
القسم الأول: الإلهيات. كالخيط المُعَلِّقِ في الهواء، تميله الرياح بلا اختيار له في شَيْءٍ أَصْلًا، وقولُ القَدَريَةِ بتأثير القدرة الحادثة في الأفعال على طبق إرادةِ العَبدِ. والجبرية كفار قطعا، لأنَّ مذهبهم ينفي التكليف الذي جاءَ بِهِ الرُّسُلُ باللأم [؟]، وفي كُفْرِ القَدَريَّةِ خِلافُ (۳) ، الأصَحُ عدَمُ كُفْرهم، لأنهم وإن لزمهم إثبات الشريكِ له تعالى ، إلا أنهم لما أثبتوا الله تعالى خلْقَ العَبدِ وقُدْرَتِهِ وإرادتِه صارَ فِعْلُ العَبْدِ في الحقيقة مخلوقا له تعالى. وعُلِمَ أيضًا أنه لا تأثير للأمور العاديّة في الأمور التي اقترنت بها، فلا تأثير للنار في الإحراق، ولا للطعام في الشبَعِ، ولا للماء في الري ولا في إنبات الزرع، ولا للكواكب في إنضاج الفواكه وغيرها، ولا للأفلاكِ في شَيْءٍ مِنَ الأَشْياءِ، ولا للسكين في القطع، ولا لشيء في دفع حرّ أو برد، أو جلبهما، أو غير ذلك لا بالطَّبع ولا بالعِلةِ ولا بقوة أودعها الله فيها، بل التأثير في ذلك كله الله تعالى وحده، بمخض اختياره عندَ وُجود هذه الأشياء.
(۱) أي لقولهم بجبرية العبد مطلقاً لأن الجبر المطلق يترتب عليه نفي التكليف ويكون إرسال الرسل عبثا، والجبرية نسبة إلى «الجبر» الذي هو نفي الفعل حقيقة عن العبد، وهذه هي الجبرية الخالصة كالجهمية، وهم الذين حكم الشيخ بكفرهم، وأما الجبرية المتوسطة فهم الذين يثبتون للعبد قدرة ولكنها غير مؤثرة أصلا، ولا ينفون التكليف، وعلى هذا يكون الأشاعرة من هذا الصنف.
(٢) أي القائلين من المعتزلة بالقدر، وهم الذين يثبتون القدر للعبد وينفونه عن الله عز وجل.
(۳) هذا ليس من كل وجه وإلا لحكم بكفرهم اتفاقا، ولكن إثبات الشريك من حيث تأثير القدرة الحادثة.
(٤) أي القدرة التي يوجد بها العبد أفعال نفسه الاختيارية ليست ذاتية منه بل هي مخلوقة لله .
(٥) الأمور العادية هي التي يجري فيها الربط بين أمرين كالنار والإحراق، إلا أن هذا الربط يصح في العقل تخلفه، وكل ما دلت عليه العادة هو الاقتران بين الأمرين، أما تأثير أحدهما في الآخر فلا دلالة للعادة عليه أصلا، ولما ثبت دليل وحدانية الأفعال علمنا أنه لا تأثير لأحد سواه تعالى في فعل من الأفعال ألبتة.
The first section: Divine matters. Like the thread hanging in the air, the winds move it with no choice for it in anything at all, and the statement of the Qadariyya about the effect of the originated power in actions according to the slave's will. The Jabriyya are disbelievers decisively, because their doctrine negates the obligation (taklif) with which the messengers came with the Lam [?]. And concerning the disbelief of the Qadariyya there is disagreement (3), the correct view is their non-disbelief, because even though it necessitates for them the affirmation of a partner to Him exalted, yet since they affirmed that Allah creates the slave's power and will, the slave's action in reality becomes created by Him exalted. And it is also known that customary things have no effect in the things with which they are conjoined: fire has no effect in burning, nor food in satiety, nor water in quenching thirst nor in causing plants to grow, nor planets in ripening fruits and other things, nor spheres in anything, nor the knife in cutting, nor anything in repelling heat or cold or bringing them, or anything else — neither by nature (tab‘) nor by causality (‘illa) nor by a power that Allah deposited in them. Rather, the effect in all that is solely Allah, by His sheer choice upon the existence of these things. (1) That is, because of their saying of the compulsion of the slave absolutely, for absolute compulsion entails negation of obligation and makes sending messengers futile. Jabriyya is attributed to 'jabr' which is the negation of the act in reality from the slave. These are the pure Jabriyya like the Jahmiyya, and they are those whom the Shaykh judged as disbelievers. As for the intermediate Jabriyya, they are those who affirm a power for the slave but it is not effective at all, and they do not negate obligation. On this, the Ash‘aris are of this type. (2) That is, those among the Mu‘tazila who affirm [human] power, and they affirm power for the slave and negate it from Allah. (3) This is not from every aspect, otherwise they would be judged disbelievers unanimously, but the affirmation of a partner is from the aspect of the effect of the originated power. (4) That is, the power by which the slave performs his voluntary actions is not intrinsic to him but is created by Allah. (5) Customary things are those in which there is a connection between two things like fire and burning, except that this connection is rationally possible to be severed. All that custom indicates is the conjunction between the two things. As for one's effect on the other, custom gives no indication of it at all. And when the proof of the oneness of acts was established, we know that none other than Him has any effect in any act whatsoever.
Source pages p. 82

Commentary
This passage begins by dividing the discussion into the first section on Divine matters. It then uses an analogy of a thread hanging in the air moved by winds without any choice, to illustrate the incapacity of created things. The author then addresses two deviant sects: the Jabriyya and the Qadariyya. The Jabriyya, who claim that the slave has no power at all, are declared outright disbelievers (kuffār qaṭ‘an) because their doctrine negates the very concept of religious obligation (taklīf) — if the slave has no choice, then commands and prohibitions are meaningless, and sending messengers would be futile. The author notes that this refers to the extreme Jabriyya (like the Jahmiyya), while the Ash‘arī position of affirming a non-effective power is a milder form. The Qadariyya, who claim that the slave's originated power (qudra ḥāditha) actually affects actions according to the slave's will, are not necessarily disbelievers. Although their view implies affirming a partner with Allah (since they give the slave independent creative power), they still affirm that Allah creates the slave's power and will, so in reality the slave's action is created by Allah. Hence, the correct position is that they are not disbelievers. The passage then establishes a universal principle: customary things have no effect whatsoever on the events associated with them. A long list of examples is given: fire does not burn by itself, food does not satisfy, water does not quench thirst nor grow plants, planets do not ripen fruits, celestial spheres do not affect anything, a knife does not cut, and nothing repels or brings heat or cold. This negation applies whether one attributes effect to nature (ṭab‘), to causal power (‘illa), or to a power deposited by Allah in the thing. Rather, the real and sole agent is Allah Ta‘ālā alone, by His sheer will, at the time of the existence of these things. The footnotes clarify: the 'customary things' (umūr ‘ādiyya) are correlations that can be severed in the mind; custom indicates only conjunction, not causation. The proof of divine unity of acts leads to the conclusion that none other than Allah has any effect.

Key Terms
الجبرية
القدرية
التكليف
القدرة الحادثة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think the Ash'ari position of affirming a non-effective power is the same as the Jabriyya's total negation of human agency.
Correction: The author distinguishes between extreme Jabriyya (kufr) and intermediate Jabriyya (like Ash'aris) who affirm a power but it is not effective, and they do not negate obligation.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why are the Jabriyya considered disbelievers?
A) They negate religious obligation (taklif).
B) They affirm a partner with Allah.
C) They deny the messengers.
D) They affirm human power.

Key Takeaway
The Jabriyya are disbelievers because they negate religious obligation, while the Qadariyya, despite their error in affirming effective human power, are not considered disbelievers because they still affirm Allah's creation of that power.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
In what areas of your life do you secretly believe that your own 'power' or 'effort' is the decisive factor, forgetting that Allah creates your ability and will? How can you cultivate a constant awareness that every action you perform is ultimately created by Him?
?
The Jabriyya's error was to deny your moral responsibility before Allah. Have you ever used the belief in predestination as an excuse to avoid obeying a difficult command or to justify a sin? What would it look like to fully embrace both Allah's decree and your personal accountability?
?
If you truly believed that your every action is a creation of Allah, how would that change the way you approach repentance, gratitude, and reliance on Him? Take a moment to thank Allah for creating even your ability to think and choose.

Negation of Natural Causality
Author negates causal efficacy of created things.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Ash'ari doctrine that only Allah has true causal efficacy, and that customary correlations are not necessary.

Core Idea
Customary things have no real effect; only Allah acts.

This lesson presents the Ash'ari principle that nothing in creation has inherent causal power. Fire does not burn by its nature, nor does food satisfy hunger. All effects are from Allah alone, by His will. This is rooted in tawḥīd al-af‘āl (oneness of acts).

Guided Path
1
Read the list of denials
Read the passage and notice the long list of examples where effect is denied: fire, food, water, planets, etc.
These are customary correlations that people assume are causal.
2
Understand the three modes of false attribution
The passage negates effect whether by nature (ṭab‘), by causality (‘illa), or by a power deposited by Allah.
This covers all possible naturalistic explanations.
3
Affirm Allah as the sole agent
The passage concludes that only Allah has effect by His sheer choice at the time of these things' existence.
This is the Ash'ari positive doctrine of tawḥīd al-af‘āl.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
القسم الأول: الإلهيات. كالخيط المُعَلِّقِ في الهواء، تميله الرياح بلا اختيار له في شَيْءٍ أَصْلًا، وقولُ القَدَريَةِ بتأثير القدرة الحادثة في الأفعال على طبق إرادةِ العَبدِ. والجبرية كفار قطعا، لأنَّ مذهبهم ينفي التكليف الذي جاءَ بِهِ الرُّسُلُ باللأم [؟]، وفي كُفْرِ القَدَريَّةِ خِلافُ (۳) ، الأصَحُ عدَمُ كُفْرهم، لأنهم وإن لزمهم إثبات الشريكِ له تعالى ، إلا أنهم لما أثبتوا الله تعالى خلْقَ العَبدِ وقُدْرَتِهِ وإرادتِه صارَ فِعْلُ العَبْدِ في الحقيقة مخلوقا له تعالى. وعُلِمَ أيضًا أنه لا تأثير للأمور العاديّة في الأمور التي اقترنت بها، فلا تأثير للنار في الإحراق، ولا للطعام في الشبَعِ، ولا للماء في الري ولا في إنبات الزرع، ولا للكواكب في إنضاج الفواكه وغيرها، ولا للأفلاكِ في شَيْءٍ مِنَ الأَشْياءِ، ولا للسكين في القطع، ولا لشيء في دفع حرّ أو برد، أو جلبهما، أو غير ذلك لا بالطَّبع ولا بالعِلةِ ولا بقوة أودعها الله فيها، بل التأثير في ذلك كله الله تعالى وحده، بمخض اختياره عندَ وُجود هذه الأشياء.
(۱) أي لقولهم بجبرية العبد مطلقاً لأن الجبر المطلق يترتب عليه نفي التكليف ويكون إرسال الرسل عبثا، والجبرية نسبة إلى «الجبر» الذي هو نفي الفعل حقيقة عن العبد، وهذه هي الجبرية الخالصة كالجهمية، وهم الذين حكم الشيخ بكفرهم، وأما الجبرية المتوسطة فهم الذين يثبتون للعبد قدرة ولكنها غير مؤثرة أصلا، ولا ينفون التكليف، وعلى هذا يكون الأشاعرة من هذا الصنف.
(٢) أي القائلين من المعتزلة بالقدر، وهم الذين يثبتون القدر للعبد وينفونه عن الله عز وجل.
(۳) هذا ليس من كل وجه وإلا لحكم بكفرهم اتفاقا، ولكن إثبات الشريك من حيث تأثير القدرة الحادثة.
(٤) أي القدرة التي يوجد بها العبد أفعال نفسه الاختيارية ليست ذاتية منه بل هي مخلوقة لله .
(٥) الأمور العادية هي التي يجري فيها الربط بين أمرين كالنار والإحراق، إلا أن هذا الربط يصح في العقل تخلفه، وكل ما دلت عليه العادة هو الاقتران بين الأمرين، أما تأثير أحدهما في الآخر فلا دلالة للعادة عليه أصلا، ولما ثبت دليل وحدانية الأفعال علمنا أنه لا تأثير لأحد سواه تعالى في فعل من الأفعال ألبتة.
The first section: Divine matters. Like the thread hanging in the air, the winds move it with no choice for it in anything at all, and the statement of the Qadariyya about the effect of the originated power in actions according to the slave's will. The Jabriyya are disbelievers decisively, because their doctrine negates the obligation (taklif) with which the messengers came with the Lam [?]. And concerning the disbelief of the Qadariyya there is disagreement (3), the correct view is their non-disbelief, because even though it necessitates for them the affirmation of a partner to Him exalted, yet since they affirmed that Allah creates the slave's power and will, the slave's action in reality becomes created by Him exalted. And it is also known that customary things have no effect in the things with which they are conjoined: fire has no effect in burning, nor food in satiety, nor water in quenching thirst nor in causing plants to grow, nor planets in ripening fruits and other things, nor spheres in anything, nor the knife in cutting, nor anything in repelling heat or cold or bringing them, or anything else — neither by nature (tab‘) nor by causality (‘illa) nor by a power that Allah deposited in them. Rather, the effect in all that is solely Allah, by His sheer choice upon the existence of these things. (1) That is, because of their saying of the compulsion of the slave absolutely, for absolute compulsion entails negation of obligation and makes sending messengers futile. Jabriyya is attributed to 'jabr' which is the negation of the act in reality from the slave. These are the pure Jabriyya like the Jahmiyya, and they are those whom the Shaykh judged as disbelievers. As for the intermediate Jabriyya, they are those who affirm a power for the slave but it is not effective at all, and they do not negate obligation. On this, the Ash‘aris are of this type. (2) That is, those among the Mu‘tazila who affirm [human] power, and they affirm power for the slave and negate it from Allah. (3) This is not from every aspect, otherwise they would be judged disbelievers unanimously, but the affirmation of a partner is from the aspect of the effect of the originated power. (4) That is, the power by which the slave performs his voluntary actions is not intrinsic to him but is created by Allah. (5) Customary things are those in which there is a connection between two things like fire and burning, except that this connection is rationally possible to be severed. All that custom indicates is the conjunction between the two things. As for one's effect on the other, custom gives no indication of it at all. And when the proof of the oneness of acts was established, we know that none other than Him has any effect in any act whatsoever.

?

The Rational Proof for Negative Attributes
Dardeer proves negative attributes via a conditional argument against temporality.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the rational proof that Allah must be described with negative attributes such as eternity, everlastingness, and others, and how their absence would imply temporality.

Core Idea
If Allah lacked negative attributes, He would be temporal—impossible for the Necessary Being.

This lesson presents the proof for Allah's negative attributes (sifat salbiyya) as expounded by Imam Dardeer. Using a conditional argument, the text demonstrates that the absence of each negative attribute would entail temporality (huduth), which is impossible for Allah. The proof is concise but powerful, grounding these attributes in pure reason.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once, including the poem line and commentary. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice the conditional structure: 'If He were not qualified... then His temporality would be necessary.'
2
Identify the negative attributes listed
The commentary enumerates five negative attributes: eternal (qadim), everlasting (baqi), not similar to temporal things, self-subsisting (qa'im bi nafsihi), and one (wahid). Note each one.
3
Examine the proof for everlastingness
The text gives a detailed proof for baqa': if Allah were not everlasting, He could cease to exist, but since He is eternal, non-existence is impossible; otherwise a specificator would be needed, implying temporality. Trace this logic step by step.
This proof exemplifies how each negative attribute is rationally necessary.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
برهان الصفات
۲۸ - لو لم يكُنْ مُتَّصِفًا بها لزِمَ * حُدوتُهُ وهُوَ مُحالٌ، فَاسْتَقِمْ -
ثُمَّ أَشار إلى بُرهانِ الصِّفاتِ السلبية إجمالًا بِقَولِه: (لو لم يكُن) أي: إنّها وجَبَ اتَّصافه بالصِّفاتِ السلبية لأنه لَوْ لَمْ يَكُنْ مُنصف السلبية بها بأن كان غير قديم أو باق، أو كان مُماثلا للحوادث، أو غَيْرَ قائم بنَفْسِه، أو غير واحدٍ فيها مرَّ، (الزم حدوثه) تعالى عن ذلك. أما القِدَمُ فظاهر. وأما البقاء فلأنه لو لم يكُن مُتَصِفًا به لَمْ يَكُنْ قديا، لأنَّ مَنْ ثَبَتَ قِدَمُه استَحالَ عَدَمُه، وإلا لكانَ جاءَ العدم، فيحتاجُ إلى مُرَجّح، وكُلِّ مُحْتاج إلى مُرَجّح حادِثٌ.
Proof of the Attributes. 28. If He were not qualified with them, His temporality would be necessary, and that is impossible, so be steadfast. Then he indicated, may Allah forgive him, to the proof of the negative attributes summarily by his saying: (If He were not) — that is, indeed it is necessary that He be qualified with the negative attributes, because if He were not qualified with the negative attributes, such as being not eternal or everlasting, or being similar to temporal things, or not self-subsisting, or not one in the way mentioned, then His temporality would be necessary, exalted is He above that. As for eternity, it is apparent. As for everlastingness, because if He were not qualified with it, He would not be eternal, since whoever's eternity is established, His non-existence is impossible; otherwise non-existence would occur, and then He would need a specificator, and everything needing a specificator is temporal.
Source pages p. 87

Commentary
This passage presents a proof for the negative attributes of Allah (sifat salbiyya). It begins with a line from the poem: 'If He were not qualified with them, His temporality would be necessary, and that is impossible, so be steadfast.' The commentary explains that this conditional argument establishes that Allah must be described with these negative attributes because otherwise He would be temporal (hadith), which is impossible. The negative attributes mentioned include: being eternal (qadim), everlasting (baqi), not similar to temporal things, self-subsisting (qa'im bi nafsihi), and one (wahid). The proof for each is sketched. Eternity (qidam) is straightforward: if He were not eternal, He would be temporal. The proof for everlastingness (baqa') is elaborated: if Allah were not everlasting, He would not be eternal, because one whose eternity is established cannot cease to exist; if non-existence were possible, a specificator would be needed to bring it about, and anything needing a specificator is temporal. Therefore, Allah must be everlasting. The overall argument is that the absence of any of these negative attributes would entail temporality, which is impossible for the Necessary Being.

البقاء
المماثلة

الوحدانية
الحدوث
المرجح

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think these attributes are arbitrarily chosen or are derived solely from revelation.
Correction: The proof shows they are rationally necessary: denying any leads to the absurdity of attributing temporality to Allah.

Checkpoint

A) Because He created the universe.
B) Because if He were not everlasting, He could cease to exist, but since He is eternal, non-existence is impossible, and a need for a cause would imply temporality.
C) Because all attributes are proven by revelation.
D) Because the Qadariyya deny it.

Key Takeaway
Allah's negative attributes are rationally necessary to negate temporality and its implications.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
The proof shows that any imperfection in Allah would lead to the absurdity of temporality. Have you ever entertained a thought about Allah that contradicts His perfection—even subtly? Search your heart: do you ever feel He is distant or indifferent, as if He changes? How will you actively guard your heart against such thoughts using what you have learned?

Divine Attributes
beginner

The Proof for Eternity (Qidam)
Proof for qidam via reductio ad absurdum.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the attribute of eternity (qidam) is proven through a reductio ad absurdum argument that avoids circularity and infinite regress.

Core Idea
Eternity is proven by showing that its opposite leads to absurdity.

Imam Dardeer begins the proof for qidam by stating that it is 'apparent'. He then provides a more elaborate argument in the footnote: if God were not eternal, He would be originated, leading to an infinite chain of causes or circularity, both impossible. Therefore, God must be eternal.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice that the main text says it is 'apparent', but the footnote provides the full argument.
2
Identify the reductio structure
The argument assumes the opposite (that God is not eternal) and shows that it leads to an absurd consequence, so the opposite must be false.
3
Understand why circularity and infinite regress are impossible
The proof shows that if God were originated, we would need an infinite chain of causes or a circular cause. Both are rationally impossible, so God cannot be originated.
This is a standard argument in Islamic theology.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أمَّا القِدَمُ فظاهِرٌ (٣). وأمَّا البَقاءُ فَلأنَّهُ لَوْ لَمْ يَكُنْ مُتَّصِفًا بِهِ لَمْ يَكُنْ قَديمًا، لأنَّ مَنْ ثَبَتَ قِدَمُهُ اسْتَحالَ عَدَمُهُ، وإلَّا لَكانَ جائِزَ العَدَمِ، فيَحْتاجُ إلى مُرَجِّحٍ، وكُلُّ مُحْتاجٍ إلى مُرَجِّحٍ حادِثٌ.
(٣) أي لَوْ لَمْ يَكُنْ قَديمًا لَكانَ حادِثًا، وَلَوْ كانَ حادِثًا لافْتَقَرَ إلى مُحْدِثٍ وهَكَذا، فَيَلْزَمُ إمَّا الدَّوْرُ وإمَّا التَّسَلْسُلُ وكِلاهُما باطِلٌ، فَبَطَلَ ما أَدَّى إلَيْهِما وهو كَوْنُهُ تَعالى حادِثًا، فَثَبَتَ نَقيضُهُ وهو كَوْنُهُ قَديمًا وهو المَطْلوبُ.
(٤) إشارَةٌ إلى قياسٍ اسْتِثْنائِيٍّ حُذِفَتْ صُغْراهُ، وتَقْريرُهُ: هكذا المولى مُتَّصِفٌ بِالبَقاءِ، لأنَّهُ لَوْ لَمْ يَكُنْ مُتَّصِفًا بِهِ لَكانَ جائِزَ القِدَمِ، وإذا كانَ جائِزَ القِدَمِ احْتاجَ إلى مُرَجِّحٍ، وكُلُّ مُحْتاجٍ إلى مُرَجِّحٍ حادِثٌ، لكنَّ كَوْنَهُ جائِزَ القِدَمِ مُحالٌ لِما تَقَدَّمَ مِن وُجوبِ وُجودِهِ تَعالى إلخ.
As for eternity, it is apparent. (3) As for everlastingness, it is because if He were not described with it, He would not be eternal, for whoever's eternity is established, his non-existence is impossible; otherwise he would be possible of non-existence, and would need a preponderator, and everything in need of a preponderator is originated. (3) That is: if He were not eternal, He would be originated, and if He were originated, He would need an originator, and so on; then either circularity or infinite regress would necessarily follow, and both are false; therefore what led to them – namely His being originated – is false, so its opposite – His being eternal – is established, and that is the desired conclusion. (4) This is a reference to an exceptional syllogism whose minor premise has been omitted. Its formulation: likewise, the Master is described with everlastingness, because if He were not described with it, He would be possible of eternity; and if He were possible of eternity, He would need a preponderator, and everything in need of a preponderator is originated; but His being possible of eternity is impossible due to what has preceded of the necessity of His existence, etc.
Source pages p. 87

Commentary
This passage proves two attributes: qidam (eternity without beginning) and baqā' (everlastingness without end). For qidam, the main text simply says 'it is apparent,' and the footnote (3) elaborates with a reductio ad absurdum: if God were not eternal, He would be originated; if originated, He would need an originator; this leads to either circularity (dawr) or infinite regress (tasalsul), both of which are impossible. Therefore, the negation is false, so eternity is established. For baqā', the proof is that if God were not described with everlastingness, then His eternal existence would be merely possible (jā'iz al-qidam), meaning He could cease to exist. But if something is possible of non-existence, it requires a preponderator (murajjih) to bring it into existence or sustain it; whatever requires a preponderator is originated (ḥādith). However, God's existence is necessary (wājib al-wujūd), not possible, so the assumption is false. Thus, He must be described with everlastingness. Both proofs rely on the principle that the Necessary Being cannot depend on anything external, nor can He be subject to non-existence.

Key Terms
قدم
حادث
دور
تسلسل

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Eternity is self-evident and requires no proof.
Correction: While Imam Dardeer states it is 'apparent,' he still provides a detailed reductio ad absurdum to show that denying eternity leads to impossible consequences.

Checkpoint
What two logical problems does the proof for qidam argue would follow if God were not eternal?
A) Dawr (circularity) and tasalsul (infinite regress)
B) Tajsim (anthropomorphism) and tashbih (comparison)
C) 'Adam (non-existence) and huduth (origination)
D) Tawhid (unity) and tawakkul (trust)

Key Takeaway
The attribute of qidam is proven by showing that its negation leads to the impossible consequences of circularity or infinite regress.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If you truly believe that Allah is eternal and uncaused, why do you sometimes act as if your existence is self-sufficient or independent of Him?
?
The argument proves that infinite regress is absurd. Have you ever allowed your worries about the future to spiral into an endless chain of 'what ifs'? How does trusting in the Eternal One cut that chain?
?
Believing in qidam means Allah alone has no beginning. What would change in your daily life if you constantly reminded yourself that everything else, including you, is originated and dependent on Him?

The Proof for Everlastingness (Baqa)
Proof for baqa via the impossibility of contingent eternity.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the attribute of everlastingness (baqa) is proven by showing that God's existence is necessary and cannot be subject to non-existence.

Core Idea
Everlastingness is proven because God's eternity cannot be merely possible; it must be necessary.

Having established that God is eternal (qidam), Imam Dardeer now proves that this eternity is not temporary but perpetual. The argument is that if God were not described with baqa, then His eternity would be merely possible (jā'iz al-qidam), meaning He could cease to exist. But anything that can cease to exist requires a preponderator to keep it in existence, and whatever depends on a preponderator is originated. Since God's existence is necessary, He cannot be possible of non-existence, so He must be everlasting.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Note the conditional structure in the main text and the syllogism in the footnote.
2
Identify the conditional chain
The argument goes: if no baqa, then jā'iz al-qidam; if jā'iz al-qidam, then needs murajjih; if needs murajjih, then originated. So no baqa leads to originated, which contradicts necessary existence.
The footnote formalizes this as an exceptional syllogism.
3
Understand why jā'iz al-qidam is impossible
God's existence is necessary (wājib al-wujūd); it cannot be merely possible. Therefore, He must have baqa.
This connects to the earlier proof of necessary existence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أمَّا القِدَمُ فظاهِرٌ (٣). وأمَّا البَقاءُ فَلأنَّهُ لَوْ لَمْ يَكُنْ مُتَّصِفًا بِهِ لَمْ يَكُنْ قَديمًا، لأنَّ مَنْ ثَبَتَ قِدَمُهُ اسْتَحالَ عَدَمُهُ، وإلَّا لَكانَ جائِزَ العَدَمِ، فيَحْتاجُ إلى مُرَجِّحٍ، وكُلُّ مُحْتاجٍ إلى مُرَجِّحٍ حادِثٌ.
(٣) أي لَوْ لَمْ يَكُنْ قَديمًا لَكانَ حادِثًا، وَلَوْ كانَ حادِثًا لافْتَقَرَ إلى مُحْدِثٍ وهَكَذا، فَيَلْزَمُ إمَّا الدَّوْرُ وإمَّا التَّسَلْسُلُ وكِلاهُما باطِلٌ، فَبَطَلَ ما أَدَّى إلَيْهِما وهو كَوْنُهُ تَعالى حادِثًا، فَثَبَتَ نَقيضُهُ وهو كَوْنُهُ قَديمًا وهو المَطْلوبُ.
(٤) إشارَةٌ إلى قياسٍ اسْتِثْنائِيٍّ حُذِفَتْ صُغْراهُ، وتَقْريرُهُ: هكذا المولى مُتَّصِفٌ بِالبَقاءِ، لأنَّهُ لَوْ لَمْ يَكُنْ مُتَّصِفًا بِهِ لَكانَ جائِزَ القِدَمِ، وإذا كانَ جائِزَ القِدَمِ احْتاجَ إلى مُرَجِّحٍ، وكُلُّ مُحْتاجٍ إلى مُرَجِّحٍ حادِثٌ، لكنَّ كَوْنَهُ جائِزَ القِدَمِ مُحالٌ لِما تَقَدَّمَ مِن وُجوبِ وُجودِهِ تَعالى إلخ.
As for eternity, it is apparent. (3) As for everlastingness, it is because if He were not described with it, He would not be eternal, for whoever's eternity is established, his non-existence is impossible; otherwise he would be possible of non-existence, and would need a preponderator, and everything in need of a preponderator is originated. (3) That is: if He were not eternal, He would be originated, and if He were originated, He would need an originator, and so on; then either circularity or infinite regress would necessarily follow, and both are false; therefore what led to them – namely His being originated – is false, so its opposite – His being eternal – is established, and that is the desired conclusion. (4) This is a reference to an exceptional syllogism whose minor premise has been omitted. Its formulation: likewise, the Master is described with everlastingness, because if He were not described with it, He would be possible of eternity; and if He were possible of eternity, He would need a preponderator, and everything in need of a preponderator is originated; but His being possible of eternity is impossible due to what has preceded of the necessity of His existence, etc.
Source pages p. 87

Commentary
This passage proves two attributes: qidam (eternity without beginning) and baqā' (everlastingness without end). For qidam, the main text simply says 'it is apparent,' and the footnote (3) elaborates with a reductio ad absurdum: if God were not eternal, He would be originated; if originated, He would need an originator; this leads to either circularity (dawr) or infinite regress (tasalsul), both of which are impossible. Therefore, the negation is false, so eternity is established. For baqā', the proof is that if God were not described with everlastingness, then His eternal existence would be merely possible (jā'iz al-qidam), meaning He could cease to exist. But if something is possible of non-existence, it requires a preponderator (murajjih) to bring it into existence or sustain it; whatever requires a preponderator is originated (ḥādith). However, God's existence is necessary (wājib al-wujūd), not possible, so the assumption is false. Thus, He must be described with everlastingness. Both proofs rely on the principle that the Necessary Being cannot depend on anything external, nor can He be subject to non-existence.

Key Terms
بقاء
جائز القدم
مرجح
حادث

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Once eternity (qidam) is proven, everlastingness (baqa) automatically follows without separate proof.
Correction: The proof shows that even if something is eternal, it could still be possible for it to cease unless its existence is necessary. Baqa is not automatically implied by qidam; it requires a separate argument based on the necessity of existence.

Checkpoint
According to the proof for baqa, what would follow if God were not described with everlastingness?
A) He would be originated
B) He would be possible of eternity (jā'iz al-qidam) and need a preponderator
C) He would be limited
D) He would be composite

Key Takeaway
Everlastingness is proven because God's existence is necessary; if it were merely possible, He would depend on something else, which is impossible.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If God's existence is absolutely necessary and everlasting, what does that mean for your own attempts to find security in temporary things? In what area of your life are you acting as if something else is necessary for your existence?
?
You have learned that God cannot cease to exist — His everlastingness is not a choice but a necessity. Does your relationship with Him reflect that reality, or do you treat Him as optional — someone you turn to only when needed?
?
Consider the proof: if God were not everlasting, He would depend on something else. Do you live as if God depends on your worship, or as if you depend entirely on Him? What needs to change in your daily life to align with this truth?
